–ü–æ –µ–≥–æ —Å–ª–æ–≤–∞–º, —Å–µ–π—á–∞—Å —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Ü—ã –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—é—Ç –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –∫–∞–∫ –º–∏–Ω–∏–º—É–º –Ω–∞ —Ç—Ä–µ—Ö –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è—Ö: —Å –∑–∞–ø–∞–¥–∞; —Å–µ–≤–µ—Ä–æ-–∑–∞–ø–∞–¥–∞, –≥–¥–µ –æ–Ω–∏ —Ä–∞—Å—à–∏—Ä—è—é—Ç –ø–ª–∞—Ü–¥–∞—Ä–º –Ω–∞ –æ–∫–∫—É–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω–æ–º \[–†–æ—Å—Å–∏–µ–π\] –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥—É —Ä–µ–∫–∏ –ò–Ω–≥—É–ª–µ—Ü; –∏ —Å —Å–µ–≤–µ—Ä–∞, –≥–¥–µ –∏–º —É–¥–∞–ª–æ—Å—å –≤–∑—è—Ç—å –∫—Ä—É–ø–Ω—ã–π –Ω–∞—Å–µ–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π –ø—É–Ω–∫—Ç –í—ã—Å–æ–∫–æ–ø–æ–ª—å–µ –∏ ¬´–∑–∞—Ç—Ä–æ—Ñ–µ–∏—Ç—å¬ª –±–æ–ª—å—à–æ–µ –∫–æ–ª–∏—á–µ—Å—Ç–≤–æ –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–π —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫–∏ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–≥–æ –¥–µ—Å–∞–Ω—Ç–∞. –ù–∞ —Å–µ–≥–æ–¥–Ω—è —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ —É–¥–∞–ª–æ—Å—å –ø—Ä–æ–¥–≤–∏–Ω—É—Ç—å—Å—è –Ω–∞ —Ç–µ—Ä—Ä–∏—Ç–æ—Ä–∏—é –±–æ–ª–µ–µ –¥–µ—Å—è—Ç–∏ –Ω–∞—Å–µ–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –ø—É–Ω–∫—Ç–æ–≤ –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –ú–∏—Ö–∞–π–ª–æ–≤. ¬´–•–æ—Ç—å —ç—Ç–∏ –Ω–∞—Å–µ–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –ø—É–Ω–∫—Ç—ã –∏ –Ω–µ–±–æ–ª—å—à–∏–µ, –æ–Ω–∏ —è–≤–ª—è—é—Ç—Å—è –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–º–∏ —É–∑–ª–∞–º–∏. –ü–æ–∫–∞ –º—ã –≤–∏–¥–∏–º –ø—Ä–µ–∏–º—É—â–µ—Å—Ç–≤–æ –Ω–∞ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω–µ¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –æ–Ω.

–ù–µ—Ö–≤–∞—Ç–∫—É —Ä–µ—Å—É—Ä—Å–æ–≤ —É —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫–∏ –Ω–∞ —ç—Ç–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –ø–æ–¥—Ç–≤–µ—Ä–∂–¥–∞–µ—Ç –∏¬†–±—ã–≤—à–∏–π —Å–æ—Ç—Ä—É–¥–Ω–∏–∫ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π —Å–ø–µ—Ü—Å–ª—É–∂–±—ã. ¬´–ò–∑-–∑–∞ –Ω–µ—Ö–≤–∞—Ç–∫–∏ —Å–æ–ª–¥–∞—Ç –∏ –æ—Ñ–∏—Ü–µ—Ä–æ–≤ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–µ –≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞ –Ω–∞ —Ñ—Ä–æ–Ω—Ç–µ —Å–æ—Å—Ä–µ–¥–æ—Ç–æ—á–µ–Ω—ã –≤ –Ω–µ–¥–æ—Å—Ç–∞—Ç–æ—á–Ω–æ–º –∫–æ–ª–∏—á–µ—Å—Ç–≤–µ. –õ—é–¥–µ–π –ø—Ä–∏–º–µ—Ä–Ω–æ –≤ —Ç—Ä–∏ —Ä–∞–∑–∞ –º–µ–Ω—å—à–µ, —á–µ–º –Ω—É–∂–Ω–æ –¥–ª—è –≤—ã–ø–æ–ª–Ω–µ–Ω–∏—è –ø–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –∑–∞–¥–∞—á: —Ç—Ä–µ–±—É–µ—Ç—Å—è –º–∏–Ω–∏–º—É–º –æ–¥–Ω–∞ –±–∞—Ç–∞–ª—å–æ–Ω–Ω–æ-—Ç–∞–∫—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∞—è –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∞ –Ω–∞ 3 –∫–∏–ª–æ–º–µ—Ç—Ä–∞, –∞ —É –†–æ—Å—Å–∏–∏ ‚Äî –æ–¥–Ω–∞ –Ω–∞ 5 –∫–∏–ª–æ–º–µ—Ç—Ä–æ–≤. –¢–∞–∫–æ–π —á–∏—Å–ª–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å—é –Ω–µ –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—é—Ç, —ç—Ç–æ –ø–æ—Ö–æ–∂–µ –Ω–∞ –∞–≤–∞–Ω—Ç—é—Ä—É, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –æ–Ω. ‚Äî –ü—Ä–æ—Ä–≤–∞–≤ –ø–µ—Ä–≤—É—é –ª–∏–Ω–∏—é \[–æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã\] —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –≤–æ–π—Å–∫, —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–µ –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ –¥–æ–ª–∂–Ω–æ –±—ã–ª–æ —É–ø–µ—Ä–µ—Ç—å—Å—è –≤–æ –≤—Ç–æ—Ä—É—é –ª–∏–Ω–∏—é, –Ω–æ –ø—Ä–æ–±–ª–µ–º–∞ –≤ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ —É —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–π –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫–∏ –µ–µ –Ω–µ—Ç: –∏–∑-–∑–∞ –Ω–µ—Ö–≤–∞—Ç–∫–∏ –ª—é–¥–µ–π —Ç–∞–∫–∏–µ –ø—Ä–æ—Ä—ã–≤—ã –∑–∞—Ç—ã–∫–∞—é—Ç –ª–∏—à—å –º–æ–±–∏–ª—å–Ω—ã–º–∏ —Ä–µ–∑–µ—Ä–≤–∞–º–∏. –ò —ç—Ç–æ –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞—Ç—å —Å–∏—Ç—É–∞—Ü–∏—é –Ω–µ–ø—Ä–µ–¥—Å–∫–∞–∑—É–µ–º–æ–π¬ª.

*   [–†–µ–∫–æ–º–µ–Ω–¥–∞—Ü—ñ—ó –¥–ª—è –∫—Ä–∏–º—á–∞–Ω ‚Äì —è–∫ –¥—ñ—è—Ç–∏ –ø—ñ–¥ —á–∞—Å –±–æ–π–æ–≤–∏—Ö –¥—ñ–π –≤ –ö—Ä–∏–º—É —Ç–∞ –¥–µ–æ–∫—É–ø–∞—Ü—ñ—ó –ø—ñ–≤–æ—Å—Ç—Ä–æ–≤–∞](https://cripo.com.ua/main/rekomendatsiyi-dlya-krymchan-yak-diyaty-pid-chas-bojovyh-dij-v-krymu-ta-deokupatsiyi-pivostrova/ "–†–µ–∫–æ–º–µ–Ω–¥–∞—Ü—ñ—ó –¥–ª—è –∫—Ä–∏–º—á–∞–Ω ‚Äì —è–∫ –¥—ñ—è—Ç–∏ –ø—ñ–¥ —á–∞—Å –±–æ–π–æ–≤–∏—Ö –¥—ñ–π –≤ –ö—Ä–∏–º—É —Ç–∞ –¥–µ–æ–∫—É–ø–∞—Ü—ñ—ó –ø—ñ–≤–æ—Å—Ç—Ä–æ–≤–∞")
    

–î–æ—Å—Ç–æ–≤–µ—Ä–Ω—ã—Ö –¥–∞–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –æ –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—è—Ö –æ–±–µ–∏—Ö —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω –≤ —ç—Ç–æ–π —Å—Ö–≤–∞—Ç–∫–µ —Å–µ–π—á–∞—Å –Ω–µ—Ç, –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –∞–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Ç–∏–∫ CIT –ö–∏—Ä–∏–ª–ª –ú–∏—Ö–∞–π–ª–æ–≤, –Ω–æ —Å—É–¥—è –ø–æ¬†[–ø—É–±–ª–∏–∫–∞—Ü–∏–∏](https://www.economist.com/europe/2022/09/04/ukraine-is-losing-fewer-soldiers-in-its-counter-offensive-than-russia-claims)
¬†The Economist (–∂—É—Ä–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Å—Ç—ã –ø–æ–±—ã–≤–∞–ª–∏ –≤ –ø—Ä–∏—Ñ—Ä–æ–Ω—Ç–æ–≤–æ–º –≥–æ—Ä–æ–¥–µ –ù–∏–∫–æ–ª–∞–µ–≤–µ, –ø–æ–≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏–ª–∏ —Å –º–µ—Å—Ç–Ω—ã–º–∏ –≤—Ä–∞—á–∞–º–∏ –∏ –Ω–µ —É–≤–∏–¥–µ–ª–∏ —Ç–∞–º ¬´–ø–µ—Ä–µ–ø–æ–ª–Ω–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –º–æ—Ä–≥–æ–≤¬ª —Å –ø–æ–≥–∏–±—à–∏–º–∏ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–º–∏ –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–º–∏, –æ —á–µ–º —É—Ç–≤–µ—Ä–∂–¥–∞–µ—Ç —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∞—è —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω–∞), —Ö–æ—Ç—å –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä–∏ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ –≤—ã—Ä–æ—Å–ª–∏ —Å –Ω–∞—á–∞–ª–æ–º –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è, –æ–Ω–∏ –Ω–µ –∫–∞—Ç–∞—Å—Ç—Ä–æ—Ñ–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏–µ, –∫–∞–∫ —ç—Ç–æ –∑–∞—è–≤–ª—è–µ—Ç —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–µ –ú–∏–Ω–æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã. –ü–æ —Å–ª–æ–≤–∞–º –±—ã–≤—à–µ–≥–æ —Å–æ—Ç—Ä—É–¥–Ω–∏–∫–∞ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π —Å–ø–µ—Ü—Å–ª—É–∂–±—ã, —Å –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–º –ø–æ–≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏–ª–∏ ¬´–í–∞–∂–Ω—ã–µ –∏—Å—Ç–æ—Ä–∏–∏¬ª, –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä–∏ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã –≤—ã—Å–æ–∫–∏, –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—é—â–∞—è —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω–∞ –≤—Å–µ–≥–¥–∞ —Ç–µ—Ä—è–µ—Ç –±–æ–ª—å—à–µ –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—è—é—â–µ–π—Å—è.

–ù–∞ —Ç—Ä–µ—Ç–∏–π –¥–µ–Ω—å –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏ The Wall Street Journal¬†[–ø–æ–≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏–ª–∞](https://www.wsj.com/articles/ukrainian-soldiers-say-they-are-advancing-in-the-south-but-at-a-cost-11661983338)
¬†–≤ –≥–æ—Å–ø–∏—Ç–∞–ª–µ —Å —Ä–∞–Ω–µ–Ω—ã–º–∏ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–º–∏ —Å–æ–ª–¥–∞—Ç–∞–º–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ —É—á–∞—Å—Ç–≤–æ–≤–∞–ª–∏ –≤ –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏–∏. –ü–æ –∏—Ö —Å–ª–æ–≤–∞–º, –±–æ–∏ –Ω–∞ –ø—É—Ç–∏ –∫ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—É –∏–¥—É—Ç –∫—Ä–∞–π–Ω–µ –æ–∂–µ—Å—Ç–æ—á–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ, –Ω–æ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–µ –≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞ –ø—Ä–æ–¥–≤–∏–≥–∞—é—Ç—Å—è –≤–ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥. ¬´–£ –Ω–∏—Ö –º–Ω–æ–≥–æ —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫–∏, –Ω–æ –º–∞–ª–æ –ª—é–¥–µ–π¬ª, ‚Äî —Å–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª –æ–¥–∏–Ω –∏–∑ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏—Ö –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö. –ö—Ä–æ–º–µ —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ, –æ–Ω–∏ —É—Ç–≤–µ—Ä–∂–¥–∞—é—Ç, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–µ–∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–µ —Å–æ–ª–¥–∞—Ç—ã –±–µ–≥—É—Ç —Å–æ —Å–≤–æ–∏—Ö –ø–æ–∑–∏—Ü–∏–π, –±—Ä–æ—Å–∞—è —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫—É –∏ —É—Å—Ç–∞–Ω–∞–≤–ª–∏–≤–∞—è –º–∏–Ω—ã –Ω–∞ —Ç–µ–ª–∞—Ö –ø–æ–≥–∏–±—à–∏—Ö —Ç–æ–≤–∞—Ä–∏—â–µ–π.

–ü–æ —Å–ª–æ–≤–∞–º –æ–¥–Ω–æ–≥–æ –∏–∑ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å–ª—É–∂–∞—â–∏—Ö, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–π —Å–µ–π—á–∞—Å –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∞—è –∞—Ä–º–∏—è —Ç–∞–º –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è –≤ —Ç—è–∂–µ–ª–æ–º –ø–æ–ª–æ–∂–µ–Ω–∏–∏, —Å–æ–ª–¥–∞—Ç—ã –º–∞—Å—Å–æ–≤–æ –ø—ã—Ç–∞—é—Ç—Å—è —É–≤–æ–ª–∏—Ç—å—Å—è. ¬´–î–≤–µ –Ω–µ–¥–µ–ª–∏ –Ω–∞–∑–∞–¥ –∫–æ–º–∞–Ω–¥–∏—Ä—ã –Ω–∞–º —Å–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª–∏, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–∞ –Ω–∞—Å –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ –∏–¥–µ—Ç. –ê –Ω–∞–º –¥–∞–∂–µ –±–æ–µ–ø—Ä–∏–ø–∞—Å—ã –Ω–∏–∫–∞–∫ –Ω–µ –ø—Ä–∏–≤–µ–∑—Ç–∏, –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ –¥–∞–º–±–∞ —Ä–∞–∑–±–∏—Ç–∞ (_–≤–µ—Ä–æ—è—Ç–Ω–æ, —Ä–µ—á—å –∏–¥–µ—Ç –æ –¥–∞–º–±–µ –≤ –ù–æ–≤–æ–π –ö–∞—Ö–æ–≤–∫–µ_¬†‚Äî¬†**–ü—Ä–∏–º. —Ä–µ–¥.**). –õ—é–¥–∏ –∫–∞–∂–¥—ã–π –¥–µ–Ω—å —Ö–æ–¥—è—Ç —Å —Ä–∞–ø–æ—Ä—Ç–∞–º–∏ \[–Ω–∞ —É–≤–æ–ª—å–Ω–µ–Ω–∏–µ\], –Ω–æ –ø–æ—á—Ç–∏ –≤—Å–µ–º –∏—Ö —Ä–∞–∑—Ä—ã–≤–∞—é—Ç¬ª, ‚Äî –Ω–∞–ø–∏—Å–∞–ª –æ–Ω. –°–ø—É—Å—Ç—è –¥–≤–µ –Ω–µ–¥–µ–ª–∏ –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π –ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥–∞–ª ¬´–í–∞–∂–Ω—ã–º –∏—Å—Ç–æ—Ä–∏—è–º¬ª, —á—Ç–æ –ø—Ä–∏ –æ–±—Å—Ç—Ä–µ–ª–µ —á—É–¥–æ–º –≤—ã–∂–∏–ª, –∏ ¬´—Ç–∞–º –≤—Å–µ –∂–µ—Å—Ç–∫–æ¬ª.

–î—Ä—É–≥–æ–π –∏—Å—Ç–æ—á–Ω–∏–∫, –±–ª–∏–∑–∫–∏–π –∫ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–º –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å–ª—É–∂–∞—â–∏–º, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥—è—Ç—Å—è –Ω–∞ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏, –ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥–∞–ª, —á—Ç–æ —Å–æ–ª–¥–∞—Ç—ã –≤ –ø–æ–ª–Ω–æ–º —à–æ–∫–µ, ¬´–Ω–∏–∫—Ç–æ –Ω–∏—á–µ–≥–æ –Ω–µ –ø–æ–Ω–∏–º–∞–µ—Ç, –≥–∏–±–Ω—É—Ç –ø–∞—á–∫–∞–º–∏, –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä–∏ —É–∂–∞—Å–Ω—ã–µ. –ù–µ–∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –≤–æ–æ–±—â–µ –∑–≤–æ–Ω—è—Ç, –ø—Ä–æ—â–∞—é—Ç—Å—è, –º—ã, –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä—è—Ç, —Å–º–µ—Ä—Ç–Ω–∏–∫–∏ –µ–±—É—á–∏–µ¬ª.

### **–£ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ –ø—Ä–æ–±–ª–µ–º—ã —Å–æ —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ–º**

–ï—â–µ –æ–¥–Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–æ–±–ª–µ–º–∞ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è –¥–æ–ª–∂–Ω–∞ —Å–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∏–≤–∞—Ç—å –ø—Ä–æ—Ä—ã–≤ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –∑–∞–∫–ª—é—á–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è –≤ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ –æ–Ω–∞ –æ–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª–∞—Å—å –æ—Ç—Ä–µ–∑–∞–Ω–Ω–æ–π –æ—Ç –≤—Å–µ—Ö –æ—Å–Ω–æ–≤–Ω—ã—Ö –ø—É—Ç–µ–π —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏—è. –†–∞–Ω–µ–µ —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫–∏ –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–º –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥—É –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä–∞ –ø—Ä–æ–∏—Å—Ö–æ–¥–∏–ª–æ —á–µ—Ä–µ–∑ –º–æ—Å—Ç—ã, –ø–æ –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–º –≤–µ–∑–ª–∏ –±–æ–µ–ø—Ä–∏–ø–∞—Å—ã, —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫—É, —Ç–æ–ø–ª–∏–≤–æ –∏ –ø—Ä–æ–¥–æ–≤–æ–ª—å—Å—Ç–≤–∏–µ —Å –ª–µ–≤–æ–≥–æ –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥–∞ —Ä–µ–∫–∏. –û–¥–Ω–∞–∫–æ –≤ —Ä–µ–∑—É–ª—å—Ç–∞—Ç–µ —É–¥–∞—Ä–æ–≤ –í–°–£ –≤—Å–µ —Å—Ç–∞—Ü–∏–æ–Ω–∞—Ä–Ω—ã–µ –º–æ—Å—Ç—ã —á–µ—Ä–µ–∑ –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä –±—ã–ª–∏ –≤—ã–≤–µ–¥–µ–Ω—ã –∏–∑ —Å—Ç—Ä–æ—è, –ø–æ–Ω—Ç–æ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –∏ –ø–∞—Ä–æ–º–Ω—ã–µ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–ø—Ä–∞–≤—ã –ø–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–Ω–æ –ø–æ–¥–≤–µ—Ä–≥–∞—é—Ç—Å—è –æ–±—Å—Ç—Ä–µ–ª–∞–º.

¬´\[–ò—Å—Ö–æ–¥ —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ –ø—Ä–æ—Ç–∏–≤–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–∏—è –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–º –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥—É –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä–∞\] –∑–∞–≤–∏—Å–∏—Ç –æ—Ç —Ç–æ–≥–æ, —É–¥–∞—Å—Ç—Å—è –ª–∏ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏—è–Ω–∞–º –æ—Ä–≥–∞–Ω–∏–∑–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å –ø–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–∫–∏ \[—Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏—è\] –ø–∞—Ä–æ–º–∞–º–∏, –ø–æ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫—É –≤—Å–µ –ø–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –º–æ—Å—Ç—ã –ø–µ—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–∞–ª–∏ —Ñ—É–Ω–∫—Ü–∏–æ–Ω–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å. –ù–∞–ª–∞–¥–∏—Ç—å –ø–æ–Ω—Ç–æ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–ø—Ä–∞–≤—ã —á–µ—Ä–µ–∑ –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä \[—Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏\] –Ω–µ —É–¥–∞–ª–æ—Å—å. –°–µ–π—á–∞—Å —Ñ—É–Ω–∫—Ü–∏–æ–Ω–∏—Ä—É–µ—Ç –Ω–µ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –ø–∞—Ä–æ–º–Ω—ã—Ö –ø–µ—Ä–µ–ø—Ä–∞–≤ ‚Äî –∏—Ö —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Ü–∞–º —Ç—è–∂–µ–ª–µ–µ –ø–æ—Ä–∞–∂–∞—Ç—å, —á–µ–º –º–æ—Å—Ç—ã, –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ –ø–∞—Ä–æ–º—ã –º–æ–±–∏–ª—å–Ω—ã, —Å–ª–æ–∂–Ω–æ –ø—Ä–µ–¥—É–≥–∞–¥–∞—Ç—å, –≥–¥–µ –æ–Ω–∏ –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥—è—Ç—Å—è.

–û–¥–Ω–∞–∫–æ –ø–µ—Ä–∏–æ–¥–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Ü—ã –ø—ã—Ç–∞—é—Ç—Å—è –ø–æ—Ä–∞–∂–∞—Ç—å —Å–∫–æ–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫–∏ –≤ –º–µ—Å—Ç–∞—Ö –æ–∂–∏–¥–∞–Ω–∏—è –ø–∞—Ä–æ–º–æ–≤. –≠—Ç–æ –¥–æ–ª–∂–Ω–æ –≤—ã–∑—ã–≤–∞—Ç—å –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ –ø—Ä–æ–±–ª–µ–º—ã —Å–æ —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ–º. –ù–∞—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫–æ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏—è–Ω–∞–º —Ö–≤–∞—Ç–∏—Ç —Ä–µ—Å—É—Ä—Å–æ–≤ –¥–ª—è –ø—Ä–æ—Ç–∏–≤–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–∏—è, –∑–∞–≤–∏—Å–∏—Ç –æ—Ç —Ç–æ–≥–æ, —Å–º–æ–≥—É—Ç –ª–∏ –æ–Ω–∏ —ç—Ñ—Ñ–µ–∫—Ç–∏–≤–Ω–æ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–±—Ä–∞—Å—ã–≤–∞—Ç—å –ø–æ–¥–∫—Ä–µ–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ, –∞ —Ç–∞–∫–∂–µ –æ—Ç —Ç–æ–≥–æ, —Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –ø—Ä–æ–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞—Ç—Å—è —Å–∏–ª—ã –í–î–í, –ø–æ–∫–∞ —É –Ω–∏—Ö –Ω–µ –∑–∞–∫–æ–Ω—á–∏—Ç—Å—è —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫–∞, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è –Ω–µ –æ—Ç–ª–∏—á–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è –±—Ä–æ–Ω–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å—é¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –∞–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Ç–∏–∫ CIT –ö–∏—Ä–∏–ª–ª –ú–∏—Ö–∞–π–ª–æ–≤.

### **–ß–µ–º –†–æ—Å—Å–∏–∏ –≥—Ä–æ–∑–∏—Ç –ø—Ä–æ–¥–≤–∏–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ –í–°–£**¬†

–û—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∏–µ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–º–∏ –≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞–º–∏ –Ω–∞—Å–µ–ª–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–≥–æ –ø—É–Ω–∫—Ç–∞ –í—ã—Å–æ–∫–æ–ø–æ–ª—å–µ –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏ 4 —Å–µ–Ω—Ç—è–±—Ä—è —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞–ª–æ –Ω–µ–≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω—ã–º –¥–ª—è —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ –≤–µ–¥–µ–Ω–∏–µ –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã—Ö –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏–π –≤ –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –ö—Ä–∏–≤–æ–≥–æ –†–æ–≥–∞ –≤ –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä–æ–ø–µ—Ç—Ä–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç –ê–ª–µ–∫—Å–∞–Ω–¥—Ä –ö–æ–≤–∞–ª–µ–Ω–∫–æ. ¬´–≠—Ç–æ –±—ã–ª–∞ –∫—Ä–∞–π–Ω—è—è —Å–µ–≤–µ—Ä–Ω–∞—è —Ç–æ—á–∫–∞, –æ—Ç–∫—É–¥–∞ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏—è–Ω–µ –º–æ–≥–ª–∏ —Ä–∞–∑–≤–µ—Ä–Ω—É—Ç—å –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—É—é –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏—é –≤ –ö—Ä–∏–≤–æ—Ä–æ–∂—Å–∫–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏. –í –Ω–∞—Å—Ç–æ—è—â–µ–µ –≤—Ä–µ–º—è —ç—Ç–∏ –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ —É –Ω–∏—Ö –æ—Ç—Å—É—Ç—Å—Ç–≤—É—é—Ç, ‚Äî –æ–±—ä—è—Å–Ω—è–µ—Ç –æ–Ω.

‚Äî –ö—Ä–æ–º–µ —Ç–æ–≥–æ, –±–ª–∞–≥–æ–¥–∞—Ä—è –í—ã—Å–æ–∫–æ–ø–æ–ª—å—é –í–°–£ –ø–æ–ª—É—á–∏–ª–∏ –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å —Ä–∞—Å—à–∏—Ä–∏—Ç—å –ø–ª–∞—Ü–¥–∞—Ä–º –≤ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–±–µ—Ä–µ–∂–Ω–æ–π —á–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –∏ —Å—Ñ–æ—Ä–º–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å —É—Å–ª–æ–≤–∏—è –¥–ª—è –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è –Ω–∞ –¥–æ—Å—Ç–∞—Ç–æ—á–Ω–æ —É–≥—Ä–æ–∂–∞—é—â–µ–º —É—á–∞—Å—Ç–∫–µ –¥–ª—è –º–Ω–æ–≥–∏—Ö –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –í–° –†–§. –ï—Å–ª–∏ –í–°–£ –±—É–¥—É—Ç –¥–æ—Å—Ç–∞—Ç–æ—á–Ω–æ —É—Å–ø–µ—à–Ω–æ —Ä–∞–∑–≤–∏–≤–∞—Ç—å –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏—è, —Ç–æ –º—ã —Å–º–æ–∂–µ–º –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç—å –æ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ –æ–≥—Ä–æ–º–Ω–æ–µ –∫–æ–ª–∏—á–µ—Å—Ç–≤–æ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –æ–∫–∞–∑–∞—Ç—å—Å—è —Ñ–∞–∫—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏ –≤ –æ–∫—Ä—É–∂–µ–Ω–∏–∏¬ª.

–°—Ç—Ä–∞—Ç–µ–≥–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏–π –∏ –ø–æ–ª–∏—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏–π —Å–º—ã—Å–ª –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏–∏ –Ω–∞ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –¥–ª—è –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—ã –≤ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã —Ä–∞–∑–≥—Ä–æ–º–∏—Ç—å —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫—É—é –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫—É –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–º –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥—É –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä–∞ –∏ –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–¥–∏—Ç—å –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω, —Å—á–∏—Ç–∞–µ—Ç –∞–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Ç–∏–∫ CIT –ö–∏—Ä–∏–ª–ª –ú–∏—Ö–∞–π–ª–æ–≤. ¬´–≠—Ç–æ –ø–æ–∑–≤–æ–ª–∏—Ç –∑–∞–¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å —ç–∫–æ–Ω–æ–º–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏–µ —Ä–µ—Å—É—Ä—Å—ã –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –∞ —Ç–∞–∫–∂–µ –ø—Ä–æ–¥–µ–º–æ–Ω—Å—Ç—Ä–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å –∑–∞–ø–∞–¥–Ω—ã–º –ø–∞—Ä—Ç–Ω–µ—Ä–∞–º –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—ã \[–ø–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤—â–∏–∫–∞–º –æ—Ä—É–∂–∏—è\], —á—Ç–æ —Å—Ç—Ä–∞–Ω–∞ –≤ —Å–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–∏–∏ –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç—å –∏ –≤—ã–∏–≥—Ä—ã–≤–∞—Ç—å ‚Äî –Ω—É–∂–Ω–æ —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –±–æ–ª—å—à–µ \[–ø–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–æ–∫\] –æ—Ä—É–∂–∏—è.

–ö—Ä–æ–º–µ —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ, –≤ –¥–æ–ª–≥–æ—Å—Ä–æ—á–Ω–æ–π –ø–µ—Ä—Å–ø–µ–∫—Ç–∏–≤–µ –ª–∏–∫–≤–∏–¥–∞—Ü–∏—è –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–±–µ—Ä–µ–∂–Ω–æ–≥–æ –ø–ª–∞—Ü–¥–∞—Ä–º–∞ —É—Å—Ç—Ä–∞–Ω—è–µ—Ç –ø–µ—Ä—Å–ø–µ–∫—Ç–∏–≤—É –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è \[—Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏\] –Ω–∞ –ù–∏–∫–æ–ª–∞–µ–≤, –ö—Ä–∏–≤–æ–π –†–æ–≥ –∏ –û–¥–µ—Å—Å—É, –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ –∏–º–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –∑–∞—Ö–≤–∞—Ç –º–æ—Å—Ç–æ–≤ –∏ –≤—ã—Ö–æ–¥ –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤—ã–π –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥ –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä–∞ –±—ã–ª —Å–∞–º—ã–º –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–º —É—Å–ø–µ—Ö–æ–º —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏—è–Ω –Ω–∞ –ø–µ—Ä–≤–æ–º —ç—Ç–∞–ø–µ –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏–∏. –õ–∏–∫–≤–∏–¥–∞—Ü–∏—è —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ –ø–ª–∞—Ü–¥–∞—Ä–º–∞ —Å–∏–ª—å–Ω–æ —Å–Ω–∏–∂–∞–µ—Ç —É–≥—Ä–æ–∑—É –≤—Å–µ–π –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–±–µ—Ä–µ–∂–Ω–æ–π –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω–µ, –≤ —Ç–æ–º —á–∏—Å–ª–µ –∑–∞–ø–∞–¥–Ω–æ–º—É –ß–µ—Ä–Ω–æ–º–æ—Ä—å—é, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–µ –∫—Ä–∏—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏ –≤–∞–∂–Ω–æ –¥–ª—è –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—ã —Å —Ç–æ—á–∫–∏ –∑—Ä–µ–Ω–∏—è, –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∏–º–µ—Ä, —ç–∫—Å–ø–æ—Ä—Ç–∞ —Å–µ–ª—å—Ö–æ–∑–ø—Ä–æ–¥—É–∫—Ü–∏–∏¬ª, ‚Äî –æ–±—ä—è—Å–Ω—è–µ—Ç —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏–º–æ—Å—Ç—å –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏–∏ –Ω–∞ —ç—Ç–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏.

–ì–¥–µ –µ—â–µ –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—é—Ç –í–°–£ –∏ –∫–∞–∫–∞—è –±–∏—Ç–≤–∞ –±—É–¥–µ—Ç —Ä–µ—à–∞—é—â–µ–π
--------------------------------------------------

–ö—Ä–æ–º–µ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –∏ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–µ–π, –í–°–£ –æ—Å—É—â–µ—Å—Ç–≤–ª—è—é—Ç –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏—è –≤ –î–æ–Ω–µ—Ü–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç –ê–ª–µ–∫—Å–∞–Ω–¥—Ä –ö–æ–≤–∞–ª–µ–Ω–∫–æ. –í —á–∞—Å—Ç–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω –Ω–∞—Å–µ–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π –ø—É–Ω–∫—Ç –û–∑–µ—Ä–Ω–æ–µ –≤ –î–æ–Ω–µ—Ü–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏. ¬´–ê–Ω–∞–ª–æ–≥–∏—á–Ω—ã–µ –Ω–æ–≤–æ—Å—Ç–∏ –±—É–¥—É—Ç –ø–æ—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç—å –∏ –∏–∑ –õ—É–≥–∞–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –≥–¥–µ –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ –∞–∫—Ç–∏–≤–∏–∑–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–ª–∏—Å—å –í–°–£, –≤–æ—Å–ø–æ–ª—å–∑–æ–≤–∞–≤—à–∏—Å—å –æ—Å–ª–∞–±–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ–º —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –ø–æ—Å–ª–µ –¥–æ—Å—Ç–∞—Ç–æ—á–Ω–æ –ø—Ä–æ–¥–æ–ª–∂–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ–≥–æ –≤–æ–∑–¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏—è –Ω–∞ –Ω–∏—Ö –æ–≥–Ω–µ–≤—ã–º –ø–æ—Ç–µ–Ω—Ü–∏–∞–ª–æ–º¬ª, ‚Äî —É–≤–µ—Ä–µ–Ω —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç.

–ü–æ –º–Ω–µ–Ω–∏—é –ö–æ–≤–∞–ª–µ–Ω–∫–æ, —Ä–µ—à–∞—é—â–µ–π –¥–ª—è —ç—Ç–æ–π –≤–æ–π–Ω—ã –±–∏—Ç–≤–æ–π —Å—Ç–∞–Ω–µ—Ç –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ –≤ –ó–∞–ø–æ—Ä–æ–∂—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏. ¬´–ë–∏—Ç–≤–∞ –∑–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–±–µ—Ä–µ–∂–Ω—É—é –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—â–∏–Ω—É ‚Äî —ç—Ç–æ –æ—á–µ–Ω—å –≤–∞–∂–Ω—ã–π –ø—Ä–æ–º–µ–∂—É—Ç–æ—á–Ω—ã–π —ç—Ç–∞–ø. –ü–æ—Å–ª–µ –µ–µ –∑–∞–≤–µ—Ä—à–µ–Ω–∏—è –∏ –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∏—è –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω–∞ –±—É–¥–µ—Ç –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∞ –∏ –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–∞—è —á–∞—Å—Ç—å —Ä–µ—Å—É—Ä—Å–æ–≤ –í–°–£, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –±—ã–ª–∏ –∑–∞–¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–æ–≤–∞–Ω—ã –¥–ª—è —Å–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∏–≤–∞–Ω–∏—è —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –æ–∫–∫—É–ø–∞–Ω—Ç–æ–≤ –∏ –¥–ª—è –≤–µ–¥–µ–Ω–∏—è —ç—Ç–æ–π –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ–π –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏–∏. –ò —ç—Ç–∏ —Ä–µ—Å—É—Ä—Å—ã –º–æ–≥—É—Ç –±—ã—Ç—å –∏—Å–ø–æ–ª—å–∑–æ–≤–∞–Ω—ã –Ω–∞ –¥—Ä—É–≥–∏—Ö –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è—Ö: –ó–∞–ø–æ—Ä–æ–∂—Å–∫–æ–π, –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π, –î–æ–Ω–µ—Ü–∫–æ–π –∏ –õ—É–≥–∞–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—è—Ö.

–û–Ω–∏ —Å—ã–≥—Ä–∞—é—Ç —Ä–µ—à–∞—é—â—É—é —Ä–æ–ª—å –≤ –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ–º —É—Å–∫–æ—Ä–µ–Ω–∏–∏, —É–≤–µ–ª–∏—á–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –∞–∫—Ç–∏–≤–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ –∏ –∏–Ω—Ç–µ–Ω—Å–∏–≤–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏–π –í–°–£. –î–ª—è –∫–æ–º–∞–Ω–¥–æ–≤–∞–Ω–∏—è —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –≤–æ–π—Å–∫ –æ—á–µ–Ω—å –≤–∞–∂–Ω–æ —Å–æ—Ö—Ä–∞–Ω—è—Ç—å –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–æ–ª—å –∏–º–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –Ω–∞–¥ –ó–∞–ø–æ—Ä–æ–∂—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å—é. –ï–µ –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—è –¥–ª—è —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏—è–Ω ‚Äî —ç—Ç–æ —Ñ–∞–∫—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏ –≤—ã—Å—Ç—Ä–µ–ª –≤ –≤–∏—Å–æ–∫, –ø–æ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫—É —ç—Ç–æ —Å—Ç–∞–Ω–µ—Ç –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä–µ–π –≤—Å–µ–≥–æ —é–≥–∞, –∞ –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—è –≤—Å–µ–≥–æ —é–≥–∞ ‚Äî —ç—Ç–æ –∏ –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—è –ö—Ä—ã–º–∞. –í—ã–π–¥—è –≤ –ó–∞–ø–æ—Ä–æ–∂—Å–∫—É—é –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å, –í–°–£ –ø–æ–ª—É—á–∞—Ç –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å –±–ª–æ–∫–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å –ö—Ä—ã–º —Å –º–∞—Ç–µ—Ä–∏–∫–æ–≤–æ–π —á–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—ã –∏ –Ω–∞–Ω–µ—Å—Ç–∏ —É–¥–∞—Ä—ã –ø–æ –ö–µ—Ä—á–µ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–º—É –º–æ—Å—Ç—É ‚Äî —Ç–æ –µ—Å—Ç—å –æ—Ç—Ä–µ–∑–∞—Ç—å –µ–≥–æ –æ—Ç –º–∞—Ç–µ—Ä–∏–∫–æ–≤–æ–π —á–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –†–æ—Å—Å–∏–∏ –∏ –Ω–∞—á–∞—Ç—å –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏—é –ø–æ –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∏—é –ö—Ä—ã–º–∞¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –æ–Ω.

¬´–ß—Ç–æ –≤–æ–π–Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–æ–∏–≥—Ä–∞–Ω–∞, –º–æ–∂–Ω–æ –±—ã–ª–æ –ª–µ–≥–∫–æ —Å—É–¥–∏—Ç—å, –∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ –Ω–µ –ø–æ–ª—É—á–∏–ª–æ—Å—å –≤–∑—è—Ç—å –ö–∏–µ–≤. –ü–ª—é—Å —Å–µ–π—á–∞—Å –Ω–∞—á–∏–Ω–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è —Å–ª—è–∫–æ—Ç—å, —Ö–æ–ª–æ–¥–∞, –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º –∑–∏–º–∞. –ò —Ç–∞–∫–∏–µ –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç—ã–µ –≤–µ—â–∏ –∫–∞–∫ —Ç–µ–ø–ª–∞—è –æ–¥–µ–∂–¥–∞, –Ω–æ—Ä–º–∞–ª—å–Ω–∞—è –æ–±—É–≤—å –∏ –º–µ—Å—Ç–æ –¥–ª—è –Ω–æ—á–ª–µ–≥–∞, –±—É–¥—É—Ç –≤–ª–∏—è—Ç—å –∫–∞–∫ –Ω–∞ –Ω–∞ –∑–¥–æ—Ä–æ–≤—å–µ, —Ç–∞–∫ –∏ –Ω–∞ –æ—Ç–Ω–æ—à–µ–Ω–∏–µ –ª—é–¥–µ–π –Ω–∞ —Ñ—Ä–æ–Ω—Ç–µ –∫ –≤–æ–π–Ω–µ, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –±—ã–≤—à–∏–π —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π. ‚Äî –≠—Ç–æ —Ç—Ä–∞–≥–∏—á–Ω—ã–π –∫–æ–Ω–µ—Ü, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–≥–æ –º—ã –∏ –æ–∂–∏–¥–∞–ª–∏. –í–æ–π–Ω–∞ —Ä–∞–±–æ—Ç–∞–µ—Ç –≤ –æ–±–µ —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã: –∑–∞ —á—Ç–æ –±–æ—Ä–æ–ª–∏—Å—å, –Ω–∞ —Ç–æ –∏ –Ω–∞–ø–æ—Ä–æ–ª–∏—Å—å. –í –Ω–∞—à–µ —Ä—É–∫–æ–≤–æ–¥—Å—Ç–≤–æ —è –Ω–µ –≤–µ—Ä—é, –∫–æ–Ω–µ—á–Ω–æ. –ö–∞–∫ —Ä–æ–¥–∏–Ω–∞ –Ω–∞—Å –∫–∏–¥–∞–µ—Ç, –º—ã –∏ —Ç–∞–∫ –∑–Ω–∞–µ–º. –£–∂–µ –∫–∏–Ω—É–ª–∞, –Ω–∞—á–∏–Ω–∞—è —Å 14-–≥–æ \[–≥–æ–¥–∞\] ‚Äî –∑–∞–∫–∞–Ω—á–∏–≤–∞—è —Å–µ–≥–æ–¥–Ω—è. –°–∞–º–∏ —ç—Ç–æ –¥–µ—Ä—å–º–æ —É—Å—Ç—Ä–æ–∏–ª–∏, –µ—Å—Ç–µ—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–æ, –º—ã –æ—Ö—É–µ—Ç—å –∫–∞–∫ –Ω–∞—Å–æ—Å–µ–º—Å—è —Ç–µ–ø–µ—Ä—å. –ü—Ä–æ–±–ª–µ–º–∞ –≤ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ –º—ã –∏–∑–Ω–∞—á–∞–ª—å–Ω–æ –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–æ–∏–≥—Ä–∞–≤—à–µ–π –∏ –Ω–µ–∫–æ–º–ø–µ—Ç–µ–Ω—Ç–Ω–æ–π —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω–µ –±—ã–ª–∏. –†–æ–¥–∏–Ω–∞ —Å–Ω–∞—á–∞–ª–∞ –∫–∏–Ω—É–ª–∞ –º—è—Å–æ–º, –∞ —Ç–µ–ø–µ—Ä—å –±—Ä–æ—Å–∏–ª–∞ —É–º–∏—Ä–∞—Ç—å. –ò —É —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ –Ω–µ—Ç –Ω–∏ —Ü–µ–ª–∏, –Ω–∏ –º–æ—Ç–∏–≤–∞, –Ω–∏–∫–∞–∫–æ–π –ø–æ–ª—å–∑—ã –Ω–∏–∫–æ–º—É ‚Äî –Ω–∏ –µ–¥–∏–Ω–æ–º—É —á–µ–ª–æ–≤–µ–∫—É¬ª.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The claim is marked as NEI when there is not enough evidence to verify the claim or if the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory. 
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `misleading`: The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the claim or image is misrepresented in a wrong context or the necessary context is omitted. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way. If the claim refers to an image, it misrepresents the origin, content and/or meaning of the image.If the claim is a text-only claim, i.e. it does not refer to an image, it misrepresents the origin, content, and/or meaning of a statement.

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

The US-based Arms Control Association said it understood US nuclear weapons strategy and posture remained the same as described in the administration‚Äôs 2022 nuclear posture review, and there had been no reorientation away from [Russia](https://www.theguardian.com/world/russia)
 and toward China.

Daryl Kimball, the executive director of the Arms Control Association, said that while US intelligence estimates suggested China might increase the size of its nuclear arsenal from 500 to 1,000 warheads by 2030, Russia currently had about 4,000 nuclear warheads ‚Äúand it remains the major driver behind US nuclear strategy‚Äù.

Biden approved the revised strategy ‚Äì called the nuclear employment guidance ‚Äì in March, according to the Times, but an unclassified notification of the policy change has not yet been presented to Congress.

After years of nuclear arms reduction efforts, the administration has been signalling willingness to expand the US arsenal to counter China and Russia‚Äôs nuclear strategies more recently. Last month, Chinese and Russian long-range bombers patrolled together near Alaska for the first time and held live-fire exercises in the South China Sea.

The second US administration official permitted to refer to the document, Vipin Narang, an MIT nuclear strategist who served in the Pentagon, said earlier this month that Biden had ‚Äúissued updated nuclear weapons employment guidance to account for multiple nuclear-armed adversaries‚Äù and for ‚Äúthe significant increase in the size and diversity‚Äù of China‚Äôs nuclear arsenal.

‚ÄúIt is our responsibility to see the world as it is, not as we hoped or wished it would be,‚Äù the Times quoted Narang as saying. [Skip to main content](#maincontent)

What Biden has done on nuclear policy while in office
-----------------------------------------------------

Biden‚Äôs most important nuclear achievement has been successfully deterring Russian nuclear escalation over the war in Ukraine: Russia has not used nuclear weapons against NATO members or against Ukraine itself. Indeed, the treaty is still standing only because Biden quickly negotiated an [extension](https://www.state.gov/on-the-extension-of-the-new-start-treaty-with-the-russian-federation/)

 interest in strategic arms control if it can find a willing partner in Moscow.

The Biden administration has also worked to stabilize relations with China, a country whose nuclear arsenal is undergoing a rapid [expansion](https://media.defense.gov/2023/Oct/19/2003323409/-1/-1/1/2023-MILITARY-AND-SECURITY-DEVELOPMENTS-INVOLVING-THE-PEOPLES-REPUBLIC-OF-CHINA.PDF)

 of Kim, ‚ÄúWill someone from his depleted and food starved regime please inform him that I too have a Nuclear Button, but it is a much bigger & more powerful one than his, and my Button works!‚Äù Trump was later [revealed](https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/donald-trump/trump-discussed-using-nuclear-weapon-north-korea-2017-blaming-someone-rcna65120)
 to have privately considered using a nuclear weapon against North Korea while falsely blaming it on another country.

Finally, the Trump administration was highly skeptical of arms control with other nuclear powers. Trump also [withdrew](https://www.nytimes.com/2018/10/19/us/politics/russia-nuclear-arms-treaty-trump-administration.html)
 the United States from the 1987 Intermediate-Range Nuclear Forces (INF) treaty, though long-standing Russian violations of the treaty deserve more blame for that than the Trump administration. This is in significant part because Biden has effectively [communicated](https://www.nytimes.com/2022/05/31/opinion/biden-ukraine-strategy.html)

Furthermore, the Biden administration has taken steps to stabilize the overall strategic nuclear relationship with Russia. It has also fortified the defense relationship with South Korea through the [Washington Declaration](https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefing-room/statements-releases/2023/04/26/washington-declaration-2/)
, which will engage the two countries more closely on nuclear deterrence matters.

What Biden might do on nuclear policy if reelected
--------------------------------------------------

As with Trump, Biden‚Äôs first term in office provides useful guidance as to his likely nuclear policy priorities were he to be reelected. ties to NATO, Japan, and South Korea, while also working to maintain lines of communication with Russia and China. Perhaps most important, Biden seems likely to carefully manage nuclear risks in the event of a serious crisis erupting with a nuclear power, for example over Taiwan, Ukraine, or the Korean Peninsula.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The claim is marked as NEI when there is not enough evidence to verify the claim or if the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory. 
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `misleading`: The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the claim or image is misrepresented in a wrong context or the necessary context is omitted. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way. If the claim refers to an image, it misrepresents the origin, content and/or meaning of the image.If the claim is a text-only claim, i.e. it does not refer to an image, it misrepresents the origin, content, and/or meaning of a statement.

* Don't state the Claim again. Rather focus on the key insights of the fact-check.
* Simply print just the summary.

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "While serving as US President in 2024, Joe Biden ordered the US forces to prepare for possible nuclear confrontations with Russia, China, and North Korea."

## Actions
```
web_search("Joe Biden orders US forces nuclear confrontation Russia China North Korea")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `web_search`
According to The Guardian, Joe Biden approved a US nuclear strategy to prepare for possible coordinated nuclear confrontations with Russia, China, and North Korea. The White House stated that the plan was approved earlier this year and was not a response to a single country or threat. (<image:2758>)

PBS News reported that Joe Biden authorized Ukraine to use U.S.-supplied long-range missiles to strike deeper inside Russia. (<image:2759>) The Brookings article discusses Biden's nuclear policy and mentions that Biden has successfully deterred Russian nuclear escalation in Ukraine and worked to stabilize relations with China.
*   [https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/article/2024/aug/20/biden-nuclear-strategy-china-threat](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/article/2024/aug/20/biden-nuclear-strategy-china-threat)
*   [https://www.pbs.org/newshour/world/biden-gives-ukraine-permission-to-use-u-s-supplied-missiles-for-deeper-strikes-inside-russia](https://www.pbs.org/newshour/world/biden-gives-ukraine-permission-to-use-u-s-supplied-missiles-for-deeper-strikes-inside-russia)
*   [https://www.brookings.edu/articles/how-would-trump-and-biden-handle-us-nuclear-policy-upon-reelection/](https://www.brookings.edu/articles/how-would-trump-and-biden-handle-us-nuclear-policy-upon-reelection/)


## Elaboration
The Guardian reports that Joe Biden approved a US nuclear strategy to prepare for possible coordinated nuclear confrontations with Russia, China, and North Korea. The White House stated that the plan was approved earlier this year.


## Final Judgement
The evidence indicates that Joe Biden, as US President, approved a nuclear strategy to prepare for potential nuclear confrontations with Russia, China, and North Korea. This information is supported by a credible source, The Guardian. Therefore, the claim is accurate. `true`


## Summary



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
According to a report in *The Guardian* ([https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/article/2024/aug/20/biden-nuclear-strategy-china-threat](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/article/2024/aug/20/biden-nuclear-strategy-china-threat)), Joe Biden approved a US nuclear strategy to prepare for possible nuclear confrontations with Russia, China, and North Korea.

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

Armed Forces Day (Poland)

From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

National holiday in Poland

| Armed Forces Day |     |
| --- | --- |
| [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Polish_M1_Abrams.jpg/330px-Polish_M1_Abrams.jpg)](/wiki/File:Polish_M1_Abrams.jpg)<br><br>Armed Forces Day 2023, Warsaw |     |
| Official name | ≈öwiƒôto Wojska Polskiego |
| Observed¬†by | Poland |
| Significance | [Battle of Warsaw (1920)](/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)") |
| Celebrations | [Military parades](/wiki/Military_parade "Military parade")<br>, equipment reviews, silences |
| Begins | 13:00 [CET](/wiki/Central_European_Time "Central European Time") |
| Date | 15 August |
| Next¬†time | 15 August 2025¬†(2025-08-15) |
| Frequency | annual |

**Armed Forces Day**, known also as the **Feast of the Polish Armed Forces** ([Polish](/wiki/Polish_language "Polish language")
: _≈öwiƒôto Wojska Polskiego_), is a national holiday celebrated annually on 15 August in Poland, commemorating the anniversary of the 1920 victory over [Soviet Russia](/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic "Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic")
 at the [Battle of Warsaw](/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)")
 during the [Polish‚ÄìSoviet War](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Polish‚ÄìSoviet War")
.[\[1\]](#cite_note-PolskieRadio2013-1)
 Armed Forces Day is held in conjunction with the [Day of the Assumption of the Virgin Mary](/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary "Assumption of Mary")
, itself a separate public holiday.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Kontakt24-2)
 The event is marked by [military parades](/wiki/Military_parade "Military parade")
, equipment reviews, showcases and remembrances by all branches of the [Polish Armed Forces](/wiki/Polish_Armed_Forces "Polish Armed Forces")
 across the country. To commemorate the republic's victory over the Red Army, Minister of Military Affairs [Stanis≈Çaw Szeptycki](/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Szeptycki "Stanis≈Çaw Szeptycki")
 established the Feast of the Soldier (_≈öwiƒôta ≈ªo≈Çnierza_), or Soldiers Day, in 1923.[\[4\]](#cite_note-4)
 In proclaiming the holiday, Szeptycki declared that, "\[o\]n the anniversary of the memorable defeat of the Bolshevik onslaught on Warsaw, we honor the memory of those killed in battles with enemies throughout all ages and for Polish independence."[\[5\]](#cite_note-Museum-5)
 The date of 15 August was chosen as it coincided with the [21st Mountain Division's](/wiki/21st_Mountain_Infantry_Division_(Poland) "21st Mountain Infantry Division (Poland)")
 evening counterattack on Russian troops, eventually forcing the Red Army's general retreat.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Kontakt24-2)
 Additionally, the government of the Second Republic desired the military's greater integration with the new state, as well as for the armed forces to improve its image among the civilian public.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Kontakt24-2)

The Feast of the Soldier remained a celebrated holiday until 1947, when the newly installed communist government of the [People's Republic of Poland](/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Poland "People's Republic of Poland")
 discontinued the tradition.[\[6\]](#cite_note-Gazeta2013-6)
 In 1950, the [Council of Ministers](/wiki/Cabinet_of_Poland "Cabinet of Poland")
 under Prime Minister [J√≥zef Cyrankiewicz](/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Cyrankiewicz "J√≥zef Cyrankiewicz")
 passed regulations to officially celebrate the military on 12 October.[\[7\]](#cite_note-DzU1950-7)
 Renaming the celebration as Polish Armed Forces Day (_Dzie≈Ñ Wojska Polskiego_), the day marked the anniversary of the Soviet-organized [Polish 1st Tadeusz Ko≈õciuszko Infantry Division](/wiki/Polish_1st_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko_Infantry_Division "Polish 1st Tadeusz Ko≈õciuszko Infantry Division")
 engaging [German](/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany")
 units at the [Battle of Lenino](/wiki/Battle_of_Lenino "Battle of Lenino")
 in October 1943.[\[7\]](#cite_note-DzU1950-7)
 The communist government found it impossible to celebrate the original date of 15 August and its coinciding historical significance, owing to its glorification of the [Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army")
's defeat.[\[8\]](#cite_note-PolskieRadio2012-8)
 Following the return of democracy in the wake of the [events of 1989](/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989 "Revolutions of 1989")
, the [Sejm](/wiki/Sejm "Sejm")
 approved the restoration of Armed Forces Day to the original 15 August date and meaning on 30 July 1992, repealing the earlier communist era 1950 declaration.[\[9\]](#cite_note-Sejm1992-9)

Commemorations
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Armed_Forces_Day_(Poland)&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: Commemorations")\
\]

Armed Forces Day is celebrated throughout Poland, with military parades, commemorations for active personnel, veterans, and the dead. As head of state and [commander-in-chief](/wiki/Commander-in-chief "Commander-in-chief")
, the [President of Poland](/wiki/President_of_Poland "President of Poland")
 presides over promotions of high-ranking officers, including the promotion of colonels to generals at the [Presidential Palace](/wiki/Presidential_Palace,_Warsaw "Presidential Palace, Warsaw")
.[\[1\]](#cite_note-PolskieRadio2013-1)
 The pageantry continues with commemorations near the [Tomb of the Unknown Soldier](/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Unknown_Soldier,_Warsaw "Tomb of the Unknown Soldier, Warsaw")
 held in [Pi≈Çsudski Square](/wiki/Pi%C5%82sudski_Square "Pi≈Çsudski Square")
.[\[11\]](#cite_note-Prezydent-11)
 The events in Warsaw typically involve the participation of the nation's political establishment, including the [president](/wiki/President_of_Poland "President of Poland")
, the [prime minister](/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Poland "Prime Minister of Poland")
, and leading members of the [cabinet](/wiki/Cabinet_of_Poland "Cabinet of Poland")
.[\[6\]](#cite_note-Gazeta2013-6)
 Leading politicians also lay wreaths at the [J√≥zef Pi≈Çsudski](/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski "J√≥zef Pi≈Çsudski")
 Monument, as well as at the [Tomb of the Unknown Soldier](/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Unknown_Soldier,_Warsaw "Tomb of the Unknown Soldier, Warsaw")
.[\[6\]](#cite_note-Gazeta2013-6)

As a [NATO](/wiki/NATO "NATO")
 member state, Armed Forces Day in Poland typically draws representatives from other allied militaries in attendance.[\[12\]](#cite_note-12)

The centennial celebrations for 2020 were "1920 Battle of Warsaw ‚Äì a Polish victory for the freedom of Europe".[\[13\]](#cite_note-13)

### Armed Forces Day Parade

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Armed_Forces_Day_(Poland)&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Armed Forces Day Parade")\
\]

One of the main attractions of the Warsaw festivities is a [military parade](/wiki/Military_parade "Military parade")
 of servicemen and women, as well as a review of existing military equipment, held normally along [Ujazd√≥w Avenue](/wiki/Ujazd%C3%B3w_Avenue "Ujazd√≥w Avenue")
.[\[11\]](#cite_note-Prezydent-11)
 Active servicemen and women participate at many events, joined often by volunteers appearing in historical dress, including those donning the equipment and dress of the [Polish‚ÄìSoviet War](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Polish‚ÄìSoviet War")
 or other historical periods.[\[1\]](#cite_note-PolskieRadio2013-1)
 The first grand military parades since the holiday was reinstated in Warsaw were in 2007 and 2008, and parades have been held yearly since 2013. In 2019, the parade took place in the southern city of [Katowice](/wiki/Katowice "Katowice")
 to honour the participation of [Silesia](/wiki/Silesia "Silesia")
's residents in the [Silesian Uprisings](/wiki/Silesian_Uprisings "Silesian Uprisings")
 from 1919 to 1921.[\[14\]](#cite_note-14)

History
-------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Armed_Forces_Day_(Poland)&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: History")\
\]

Main article: [Battle of Warsaw (1920)](/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)")

In the event known by the critics as the "Miracle of the Vistula," the [Polish Army](/wiki/Polish_Army "Polish Army")
 under the command of Marshal [J√≥zef Pi≈Çsudski](/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski "J√≥zef Pi≈Çsudski")
 successfully repulsed a [Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army")
 offensive outside of Warsaw in mid-August 1920. As the day coincides with the religious [Day of the Assumption](/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary "Assumption of Mary")
, church masses across the country reflect on the memory of Poland's military dead.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Kontakt24-2)
 Additionally, a number of military-themed events are held throughout many of the nation's larger towns and cities, including equipment demonstrations for the general public and open house events.[\[10\]](#cite_note-TVNWarszawa-10)

In Warsaw, the holiday is commemorated by several state events in the central [≈ör√≥dmie≈õcie](/wiki/%C5%9Ar%C3%B3dmie%C5%9Bcie,_Warsaw "≈ör√≥dmie≈õcie, Warsaw")
 borough of the capital."

# Record
## Claim

### Evidence from `web_search`
The Associated Press reported on Poland's military parade on August 15, 2024, which was part of the annual Armed Forces Day observances in Warsaw, Poland (<image:25>). The Polish Ministry of Defence announced a military parade on August 15, 2024, as part of a four-day celebration from August 14 to 17, showcasing military hardware and expressing "strength, agency and unity" in the face of "threats from the East" (<image:25>).

## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The claim is marked as NEI when there is not enough evidence to verify the claim or if the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory. 
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `misleading`: The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the claim or image is misrepresented in a wrong context or the necessary context is omitted. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way. If the claim refers to an image, it misrepresents the origin, content and/or meaning of the image.If the claim is a text-only claim, i.e. it does not refer to an image, it misrepresents the origin, content, and/or meaning of a statement.

## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

# Example: geolocate()

Ukraine Has Reportedly Lost About 40 Leopard Tanks Since February 2022
======================================================================

[10:12 17.10.2024](/20241017/ "News archive")
 (Updated: 13:02 17.10.2024)

¬© AP Photo / Michael SohnA Leopard 2 tank as a part of weapons deliveries to Ukraine

![A Leopard 2 tank as a part of weapons deliveries to Ukraine - Sputnik Africa, 1920, 17.10.2024](https://cdn1.img.sputniknews.africa/img/07e8/07/0d/1067487443_0:0:3564:2004_1920x0_80_0_0_7733207e8d6471ece40fd505c0b45362.jpg "A Leopard 2 tank as a part of weapons deliveries to Ukraine")

¬© AP Photo / Michael Sohn

Subscribe

MOSCOW (Sputnik) - Ukraine has lost around 40 Leopard tanks since the beginning of Russia's special military operation in February 2022, the Business Insider news outlet reported on Thursday.

Some open-source estimates suggest that Ukraine had already [lost](https://en.sputniknews.africa/20241013/1068665538.html)
 nearly 40 Leopards, but those estimates are unconfirmed so far, according to the report.

Russia repeatedly stated that arms supplies to Ukraine hinder the settlement and directly involve NATO countries in the conflict. Russian Foreign Minister Sergey Lavrov said that the United States and [NATO](https://en.sputniknews.africa/20240512/1066501213.html)
 were directly involved in the conflict not only by providing weapons but also by training Ukrainian personnel in European countries.

[![Leopard 2 and Bradley pictured among destroyed and damaged Ukrainian vehicles. Screenshot of Russian Defense Ministry video. - Sputnik Africa, 1920, 04.11.2023](https://cdn1.img.sputniknews.africa/img/07e7/08/05/1061086329_0:221:1360:765_1920x0_80_0_0_e3c9d50c9e4682697a50f5d445b1b805.jpg "Leopard 2 and Bradley pictured among destroyed and damaged Ukrainian vehicles. Screenshot of Russian Defense Ministry video.")](/20231104/quarter-of-leopard-2-tanks-written-off-by-ukraine-just-over-week-1063322121.html "Quarter of Leopard 2 Tanks 'Written Off' by Ukraine Just Over Week")

By [AFP](https://www.themoscowtimes.com/author/afp "AFP")

June 13, 2023

! <image:2769>

Ukrainian Armed Forces destroyed in the Zaporozhye direction. Russian Defence Ministry / TASS

Moscow said Tuesday that it had captured several German Leopard tanks and U.S. Bradley infantry fighting vehicles, releasing footage showing Russian troops surveying the equipment supplied to Ukraine by Western countries.

"Leopard tanks and Bradley infantry fighting vehicles. These are our trophies. Equipment of the Ukrainian armed forces in the Zaporizhzhia region," the Russian Defense Ministry said in a statement.

"Servicemen of the Vostok group inspect enemy tanks and infantry fighting vehicles captured in battle."

Kyiv has appealed to its allies in the West to deliver a broad range of modern military equipment to help Ukrainian forces recapture large swathes of territory controlled by Russian forces.

The Defense Ministry said several of the captured vehicles had working engines, suggesting that the battles they were involved in had been short and that Ukrainian troops had "fled" their offensive positions.

**(DEFENCE SECURITY ASIA) ‚Äî During the week of May 11 to 17, Russian military claimed to have successfully destroyed five Leopard 2A1 tanks, manufactured by the German company Krauss-Maffei but donated to the Ukrainian Armed Forces to help the Eastern Europe country in its armed conflict with Russia.**

**In addition to the Leopard tanks, the Russian Ministry of Defense also alleged that 13 armored vehicles, 55 various vehicles, ‚ÄúGrad‚Äù multiple rocket launcher systems, and 47 artillery units‚Äî22 of which were supplied by foreign countries‚Äîwere destroyed during this period.**

**Moreover, four Mi-24 helicopters and 40 unmanned boats belonging to the Ukrainian military were reportedly destroyed by Russia in the same timeframe.**

**Among the foreign-supplied armored vehicles to Ukraine, the Leopard tanks have been the most frequently supplied to Kyiv compared to other models such as the American-made Abrams and the British-made Challengers.**

**Since last year, countries such as Germany and several other European nations have supplied between 100-200 Leopard tanks to Ukraine for use in a spring counteroffensive against Russian positions.**

**‚ÄúRussian Soldiers Pose in Front of Captured Leopard 2A6 Tank‚Äù**

**Line of Leopard tanks and Bradley armoured infantry fighting vehicle were destroyed in Zaphorizia, southern Ukraine.**

**Although the Ukrainian counteroffensive in 2023 initially started well, it faced increasingly formidable opposition from Russian forces who began altering their tactics and strategies.**

**These changes in strategy and tactics by the Russian forces led to the destruction of many of the Ukrainian tanks that had been supplied by donor countries like Germany, other European nations, the United States, and Britain.**

**However, to date, no one knows exactly how many Leopard tanks have been destroyed by Russia.**

**Nevertheless, Russian President Vladimir Putin has reportedly stated to his country‚Äôs war correspondents that Ukraine has lost more than 160 tanks supplied by foreign countries.**

**Given the high volume of Leopard tanks supplied to Ukraine, it is logical to conclude that many of the tanks destroyed by Russia were Leopard models.**

**Regarding the Abrams tanks, the Russian military stated that of the 31 American-made tanks supplied to Ukraine, more than five of the tanks have been destroyed by Russian forces.**

**A charred M1A1 Abrams main battle tank being transported to Moscow to participate in an exhibition at Victory Park.**

¬†**As a result of the destruction of five Abrams tanks, the United States has reportedly ‚Äúwithdrawn‚Äù these tanks from the Ukrainian battlefield, likely in an effort to ‚Äúpreserve its reputation.‚Äù**

**Following the destruction experienced by Leopard tanks supplied by Germany and other European countries, Ukraine‚Äôs Deputy Foreign Minister Andii Melnyk has requested that Kiev be supplied with more Leopard tanks, including the latest variant, the Leopard 2A6.**

¬†**However, the newest Leopard 2A6 variant supplied to Ukraine has met the same fate.**

**The Russian military reported capturing the most powerful tank in the Ukrainian arsenal, the German-made Leopard 2A6, after intense fighting in Avdiivka, Ukraine, last April.**

**It is believed that Ukraine possesses 21 Leopard 2A6 tanks, with 18 of these tanks developed by the companies Krauss-Maffei Wegmann and Rheinmetall being donated by Germany, while the remainder were provided by Portugal.**

**However, most of these Leopard 2A6 tanks donated to the Ukrainian military could not be used after failing to be properly maintained and remained inoperable as claimed by a senior German politician last January.**

**An Abrams tank caught fire after being struck by a Lancet kamikaze drone and an RPG from Russian forces.**

**According to Russian military sources, after capturing and removing the tank from the combat area, Russian forces transported the tank and sent it to Moscow, possibly for research purposes.**

**The Leopard 2A6 was successfully captured after a Russian platoon executed an ambush that caused the Ukrainian tank crew to abandon the German-made vehicle.**

**The Leopard 2A6 represents an upgrade from the Leopard 2A5, incorporating enhanced armor protection, firepower, and electronic warfare capabilities.**

**The tank measures 9.97 meters in length and weighs 62.3 tons, making it one of the heaviest main battle tanks ever deployed, with an engine power of 1,500 horsepower.**

**Capable of speeds up to 75 km/h and with an operational range of 500 km, it is equipped with a Rheinmetall 120 mm L/55 cannon, allowing it to fire all standard NATO ammunition types, including APFSDS, HEAT, and multi-purpose shells.**

**The Leopard 2A6 also features dual 7.62 mm MG3A1 machine guns and an advanced fire control system including a laser rangefinder, thermal imaging, and a ballistic computer. ‚Äî DSA**

[![North Korea](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Flag_of_North_Korea.svg/40px-Flag_of_North_Korea.svg.png)](/wiki/North_Korea "North Korea")
 600 killed, 4,100 injured, 2 captured**Per Russia:** 358 civilians killed, 503 injured[\[33\]](#cite_note-mt288-34)
 and 789 civilians missing [\[34\]](#cite_note-g266-35)
  
144,000+ civilians evacuated[\[35\]](#cite_note-mt133-36)
 (133,000+ evacuated in Kursk Oblast and 11,000+ evacuated in Belgorod Oblast)[\[35\]](#cite_note-mt133-36)
[\[36\]](#cite_note-37)

On 6 August 2024, during the [Russian invasion of Ukraine](/wiki/Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "Russian invasion of Ukraine")
,[\[37\]](#cite_note-dw.com-38)
[\[38\]](#cite_note-ft.com-39)
\[_[failed verification](/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability "Wikipedia:Verifiability")\
 ‚Äì [see discussion](/wiki/Talk:Kursk_campaign#A_ridiculous_edit "Talk:Kursk campaign")\
_\] part of the [Russo-Ukrainian War](/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War "Russo-Ukrainian War")
, the [Armed Forces of Ukraine](/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Ukraine "Armed Forces of Ukraine")
 launched an incursion into [Russia](/wiki/Russia "Russia")
's [Kursk Oblast](/wiki/Kursk_Oblast "Kursk Oblast")
 and clashed with the [Russian Armed Forces](/wiki/Russian_Armed_Forces "Russian Armed Forces")
 and [Russian border guard](/wiki/FSB_Border_Service_of_Russia "FSB Border Service of Russia")
.[\[39\]](#cite_note-REU86-40)
[\[37\]](#cite_note-dw.com-38)
[\[38\]](#cite_note-ft.com-39)
 A [state of emergency](/wiki/State_of_emergency_in_Russia "State of emergency in Russia")
 was declared in Kursk Oblast,[\[40\]](#cite_note-BBC_8_Aug-41)
 and Russian reserves were rushed to the area.[\[41\]](#cite_note-BBC_Cursino-42)
 By the end of the first week, the Ukrainian military said it had captured 1,000¬†km2 (390¬†sq¬†mi) of Russian territory, while Russian authorities acknowledged that Ukraine had captured 28 settlements.[\[42\]](#cite_note-43)

In the second half of August the front stabilized,[\[43\]](#cite_note-forbes_20240911-44)
 and in early October, the Ukrainian advance had stalled.[\[11\]](#cite_note-CNN_Third_Month-12)
 From November, North Korean forces were sent to the province to support the Russian military. By the end of August, the operation began to be criticized for diverting Ukrainian forces from [the east](/wiki/Eastern_Ukraine_campaign "Eastern Ukraine campaign")
, stretching Ukraine's personnel along the front and allowing Russia to [advance toward Pokrovsk](/wiki/Pokrovsk_offensive "Pokrovsk offensive")
.[\[47\]](#cite_note-AlexHorton-48)
[\[48\]](#cite_note-Miller-49)
 The [Institute for the Study of War](/wiki/Institute_for_the_Study_of_War "Institute for the Study of War")
 reported that Russia had moved forces from "lower-priority" areas, but not from Donetsk Oblast.[\[49\]](#cite_note-50)

The Ukrainian incursion into Kursk surprised Russia, some of Ukraine's allies, and many in the Ukrainian elite.[\[41\]](#cite_note-BBC_Cursino-42)
[\[50\]](#cite_note-ap_20240814-51)
[\[51\]](#cite_note-guardiansept-52)
 It is the most significant attack across the border since the 2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine,[\[52\]](#cite_note-53)
 and the first carried out primarily by Ukrainian regular forces. According to Russia, the incursion involved around 300 Ukrainian troops, 11 tanks, and over 20 [armored combat vehicles](/wiki/Armoured_fighting_vehicle "Armoured fighting vehicle")
,[\[68\]](#cite_note-MT86-69)
 and was aimed in two directions: at [Oleshnya](/wiki/Oleshnya,_Kursk_Oblast "Oleshnya, Kursk Oblast")
 in the direction of [Sudzha](/wiki/Sudzha "Sudzha")
, east-northeast of [Sumy](/wiki/Sumy "Sumy")
, and towards [Nikolayevo-Darino](/wiki/Nikolayevo-Darino "Nikolayevo-Darino")
, north-northeast of Sumy.[\[69\]](#cite_note-ISW_August_6-70)
 It was reported that Chechen [Akhmat battalions](/wiki/Russian_irregular_units_in_Ukraine#Akhmat_battalions "Russian irregular units in Ukraine")
 were responding to the raids,[\[69\]](#cite_note-ISW_August_6-70)
 though these claims remained unverified as of 13 September 2024.[\[70\]](#cite_note-71)

The attack began at 08:00 [MSK](/wiki/Moscow_Time "Moscow Time")
. [Alexei Smirnov](/wiki/Alexei_Smirnov_(politician) "Alexei Smirnov (politician)")
, acting [governor of Kursk Oblast](/wiki/Governor_of_Kursk_Oblast "Governor of Kursk Oblast")
, reported that three people died during the events: a woman in the border incursion and two individuals in separate drone attacks.[\[71\]](#cite_note-72)
 Russian [milbloggers](/wiki/Milblog "Milblog")
 also largely dismissed the supposed raids as "unsuccessful" and a "media stunt".[\[69\]](#cite_note-ISW_August_6-70)

According to Russia, at least 1,000 troops crossed the border on the first day, supported by [tanks](/wiki/Tank "Tank")
 and armored vehicles.[\[40\]](#cite_note-BBC_8_Aug-41)
 According to Andrzej Wilk of the [Centre for Eastern Studies](/wiki/Centre_for_Eastern_Studies "Centre for Eastern Studies")
, the entire Ukrainian grouping, including some elements which did not cross over into Russia, consisted of an estimated 2,000 men from Ukraine's [22nd](/wiki/22nd_Mechanized_Brigade_(Ukraine) "22nd Mechanized Brigade (Ukraine)")
 and [82nd](/wiki/82nd_Air_Assault_Brigade_(Ukraine) "82nd Air Assault Brigade (Ukraine)")
 Brigades, supported by artillery and air defense sub-units.[\[67\]](#cite_note-wilk-68)
 It was later claimed by members of the Ukrainian military that the breakthrough on the border was conducted by the 80th and 82nd Air Assault Brigades.[\[65\]](#cite_note-Kyrylenko-66)

Russian milbloggers claimed that the offensive was being performed by the [Russian Volunteer Corps](/wiki/Russian_Volunteer_Corps "Russian Volunteer Corps")
 (RVC), while the _[New Voice of Ukraine](/wiki/New_Voice_of_Ukraine "New Voice of Ukraine")
_ citing a source in [Ukraine's Main Military Intelligence](/wiki/Ukraine%27s_Main_Military_Intelligence "Ukraine's Main Military Intelligence")
 reported that the RVC was not present.[\[69\]](#cite_note-ISW_August_6-70)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%A1%D0%A3_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg/250px-%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%A1%D0%A3_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B2%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B4%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%A1%D0%A3_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%8E_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C.jpg)

Building damaged in Kursk Oblast, 6¬†August 2024

#### 7 August

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Ukrainian_%22Southern_Railway%22_1943.jpg/250px-Ukrainian_%22Southern_Railway%22_1943.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ukrainian_%22Southern_Railway%22_1943.jpg)

1943 Ukrainian railway map shows Sudzha in quadrant A2 at km 60 on the [Lgov](/wiki/Lgov,_Kursk_Oblast "Lgov, Kursk Oblast")
‚Äì[Gotnya](/wiki/Gotnya "Gotnya")
‚Äì[Zolochiv](/wiki/Zolochiv,_Kharkiv_Oblast "Zolochiv, Kharkiv Oblast")
 main line to [Kharkiv](/wiki/Kharkiv "Kharkiv")

A milblogger claimed that Ukrainian forces had captured 11 settlements and had advanced 14 kilometres (9¬†mi) deep into the oblast.[\[72\]](#cite_note-NBC87-73)
 Government agencies were ordered by President [Vladimir Putin](/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin")
 to "provide the needed assistance to residents", and deputy prime minister [Denis Manturov](/wiki/Denis_Manturov "Denis Manturov")
 was sent to oversee their work.[\[73\]](#cite_note-mt1-74)
 Kursk Oblast was placed under a [state of emergency](/wiki/State_of_emergency "State of emergency")
 by governor Smirnov.[\[74\]](#cite_note-dw1-75)
[\[75\]](#cite_note-CNBC_State_of_Emergency-76)

Putin met with key members of the security establishment including [Valery Gerasimov](/wiki/Valery_Gerasimov "Valery Gerasimov")
, [Alexander Bortnikov](/wiki/Alexander_Bortnikov "Alexander Bortnikov")
, [Sergei Shoigu](/wiki/Sergei_Shoigu "Sergei Shoigu")
 and [Andrey Belousov](/wiki/Andrey_Belousov "Andrey Belousov")
 on the Kursk incursion.[\[76\]](#cite_note-kru1-77)
 Gerasimov told Putin that about 1,000 Ukrainian soldiers took part in the attack and that their advance had been halted.[\[75\]](#cite_note-CNBC_State_of_Emergency-76)
[\[77\]](#cite_note-Reuters_Videos_show_Ukrainian_Presence-78)

Geolocated footage confirmed that Ukrainian forces had advanced at least 10 kilometres (6.2¬†mi) across the Russian border, having penetrated at least two Russian defensive lines and a stronghold. Additionally, there were reports of fighting in [Ivnitsa](/w/index.php?title=Ivnitsa&action=edit&redlink=1 "Ivnitsa (page does not exist)")
¬†\[[ru](https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%98%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0_(%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C) "ru:–ò–≤–Ω–∏—Ü–∞ (–ö—É—Ä—Å–∫–∞—è –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å)")\
; [uk](https://uk.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%86%D0%B2%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D1%8F_(%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C) "uk:–Ü–≤–Ω–∏—Ü—è (–ö—É—Ä—Å—å–∫–∞ –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å)")\
\], a village 24¬†km (15¬†mi) from the border.[\[80\]](#cite_note-Politico_August_8-81)
 Russian sources claimed that Ukrainian forces had reached the village of [Darino](/wiki/Darino,_Kursk_Oblast "Darino, Kursk Oblast")
.[\[81\]](#cite_note-82)

#### 8 August

[RIA Novosti](/wiki/RIA_Novosti "RIA Novosti")
 reported that four people died as a result of 'attacks' by the [AFU](/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Ukraine "Armed Forces of Ukraine")
 in the oblast[\[82\]](#cite_note-Rai_2024-08-08-2-83)
 as fighting continued for the third day.[\[83\]](#cite_note-Reuters_2024-08-08-84)
[\[84\]](#cite_note-AlJazeera_2024-08-08-85)
 Pro-Russian milblogger Yuri Podolyaka said that "Sudzha is basically lost to us" and that Ukrainian forces were pushing towards [Lgov](/wiki/Lgov,_Kursk_Oblast "Lgov, Kursk Oblast")
.[\[85\]](#cite_note-86)

Ukrainian forces were in control of the western part of Sudzha and the surrounding roads; skirmishes continued in the town.[\[86\]](#cite_note-agent-87)

According to Smirnov, the acting governor of Kursk Oblast, six Ukrainian drones and five missiles were shot down during the night and morning.[\[87\]](#cite_note-meduzalive8aug-88)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/President_Vladimir_Putin_talks_with_the_governor_of_Kursk_in_August_2024.jpg/250px-President_Vladimir_Putin_talks_with_the_governor_of_Kursk_in_August_2024.jpg)](/wiki/File:President_Vladimir_Putin_talks_with_the_governor_of_Kursk_in_August_2024.jpg)

[Vladimir Putin](/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin")
 talks with [Alexei Smirnov](/wiki/Alexei_Smirnov_(politician) "Alexei Smirnov (politician)")
, the acting [governor of Kursk](/wiki/Governor_of_Kursk_Oblast "Governor of Kursk Oblast")
, about the situation regarding the Ukrainian incursion. As a result of the UAV attack, Kurchatov, as well as parts of the [Kurchatovsky](/wiki/Kurchatovsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Kurchatovsky District, Kursk Oblast")
, [Oktyabrsky](/wiki/Oktyabrsky,_Lgovsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Oktyabrsky, Lgovsky District, Kursk Oblast")
, [Bolshesoldatsky](/wiki/Bolshesoldatsky "Bolshesoldatsky")
, [Oboyansky](/wiki/Oboyansky "Oboyansky")
 and [Belovsky](/wiki/Belovsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Belovsky District, Kursk Oblast")
 districts, were left without power supply.[\[106\]](#cite_note-107)

A counter-terrorism operational regime under the [Federal Security Service](/wiki/Federal_Security_Service "Federal Security Service")
, headed by [Alexander Bortnikov](/wiki/Alexander_Bortnikov "Alexander Bortnikov")
,[\[5\]](#cite_note-ISW_2024-08-10-6)
 was introduced in [Kursk](/wiki/Kursk_Oblast "Kursk Oblast")
, [Bryansk](/wiki/Bryansk_Oblast "Bryansk Oblast")
 and [Belgorod Oblasts](/wiki/Belgorod_Oblast "Belgorod Oblast")
 to temporarily take control of the regions till the conditions return to normalcy.[\[107\]](#cite_note-108)
 This meant that movement was restricted, vehicles could be seized, and phone calls could be monitored, among other measures.[\[108\]](#cite_note-voa1-109)

The number of Ukrainian troops in Kursk Oblast was estimated by [CEIP](/wiki/Carnegie_Endowment_for_International_Peace "Carnegie Endowment for International Peace")
 senior fellow Dara Massicot to be around 10,000‚Äì12,000, containing elements from four to five Ukrainian brigades.[\[109\]](#cite_note-110)

#### 10 August

According to analysts cited by _[The New York Times](/wiki/The_New_York_Times "The New York Times")
_, the Ukrainian advance in Kursk Oblast had largely been stopped by Russian reinforcements at this point, and the situation stabilized, but Ukrainian forces continued to hold on to their captured territory.[\[110\]](#cite_note-111)
 Conversely, other sources such as the _[Washington Post](/wiki/Washington_Post "Washington Post")
_ and _[Frankfurter Rundschau](/wiki/Frankfurter_Rundschau "Frankfurter Rundschau")
_ reported that Russia remained unable to control the situation, with continued Ukrainian advances.[\[111\]](#cite_note-Khurshudyan810-112)
[\[112\]](#cite_note-113)
 The [Russian Ministry of Defense](/wiki/Russian_Ministry_of_Defense "Russian Ministry of Defense")
 made similar claims that they had stopped any Ukrainian advances in Kursk Oblast.[\[113\]](#cite_note-114)
 Russian authorities introduced a "counter-terrorist operation" regime in Kursk Oblast.[\[114\]](#cite_note-115)
[\[108\]](#cite_note-voa1-109)

Battles were reported in [Olgovka](/wiki/Olgovka,_Kursk_Oblast "Olgovka, Kursk Oblast")
 near Korenevo, the Ivashkovskoye farmstead, and Malaya Loknya.[\[115\]](#cite_note-116)

On 10 August, Ukraine's [95th Air Assault Brigade](/wiki/95th_Air_Assault_Brigade "95th Air Assault Brigade")
 entered Kursk Oblast, and was given the task of conducting assaults and mop-up operations around [Malaya Loknya](/wiki/Malaya_Loknya "Malaya Loknya")
 and [Pogrebki](/w/index.php?title=Pogrebki&action=edit&redlink=1 "Pogrebki (page does not exist)")
¬†\[[ru](https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BA%D0%B8_(%D0%9A%D1%83%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C) "ru:–ü–æ–≥—Ä–µ–±–∫–∏ (–ö—É—Ä—Å–∫–∞—è –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å)")\
\].[\[65\]](#cite_note-Kyrylenko-66)

The Russian Armed Forces claimed to have regained control of the village of Makhnovka east of Sudzha.[\[116\]](#cite_note-117)
 Reports claimed that the combat zone had expanded to 650¬†km2 (250¬†sq¬†mi).[\[117\]](#cite_note-118)

In the evening, Kursk Oblast governor Smirnov said that 15 people were injured in Kursk city after the wreckage of an intercepted Ukrainian missile fell onto a residential area.[\[118\]](#cite_note-BBC_Tough_Response-119)

Soldiers of Ukraine's [252nd Territorial Defense Battalion](/wiki/241st_Territorial_Defense_Brigade_(Ukraine) "241st Territorial Defense Brigade (Ukraine)")
 published footage from Poroz, a border village in [Belgorod Oblast](/wiki/Belgorod_Oblast "Belgorod Oblast")
.[\[111\]](#cite_note-Khurshudyan810-112)

#### 11 August

On the night of 11 August, the Ukrainian Armed Forces entered [Belovsky District](/wiki/Belovsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Belovsky District, Kursk Oblast")
, located southeast of Sudzhansky District, which was confirmed by the head of the district and the acting governor. Russian officials said that the loss of the bridge would hinder the relocation via land routes of civilians in the district.[\[152\]](#cite_note-153)
[\[153\]](#cite_note-154)
 Approximately 2,000 to 3,000 Russian conscripts were trapped in a [pocket](/wiki/Pocket_(military) "Pocket (military)")
 south of the river.[\[154\]](#cite_note-155)

#### 17 August

Russian forces reportedly blew up two bridges near [Tyotkino](/wiki/Tyotkino "Tyotkino")
 and [Popovo-Lezhachi](/wiki/Popovo-Lezhachi "Popovo-Lezhachi")
 after withdrawing from the right bank of the [Seym River](/wiki/Seym_River "Seym River")
 in the area.[\[155\]](#cite_note-156)

The Ukrainian military claimed the capture of the settlement of [Korenevo](/wiki/Korenevo,_Korenevsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Korenevo, Korenevsky District, Kursk Oblast")
 but the Russian MOD described the settlement as contested.[\[156\]](#cite_note-157)

#### 18 August

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/The_80th_Air_Assault_Brigade_captured_a_T-90M_Proryv_tank_in_the_Kursk_region.jpg/250px-The_80th_Air_Assault_Brigade_captured_a_T-90M_Proryv_tank_in_the_Kursk_region.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_80th_Air_Assault_Brigade_captured_a_T-90M_Proryv_tank_in_the_Kursk_region.jpg)

Ukrainian soldiers with a captured Russian [T-90](/wiki/T-90 "T-90")
M Proryv tank

Ukrainian forces destroyed another bridge over the [Seym](/wiki/Seym_(river) "Seym (river)")
 river near [Zvannoye](/wiki/Zvannoye "Zvannoye")
.[\[157\]](#cite_note-158)
[\[158\]](#cite_note-ISW_2024-08-16-159)
[\[159\]](#cite_note-160)

According to Russian bloggers, both Ukraine and Russia reinforced their forces battling in Kursk Oblast, with Russia moving some forces from other fronts to the front.[\[160\]](#cite_note-newsweek20240818-161)
\[_[better¬†source¬†needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS "Wikipedia:NOTRS")\
_\]

Marines from the [501st Separate Naval Infantry Battalion](/wiki/501st_Separate_Naval_Infantry_Battalion "501st Separate Naval Infantry Battalion")
 posted a video of them tearing down the Russian flag from the municipal building of [Apanasovka](/wiki/Apanasovka,_Korenevsky_District,_Kursk_Oblast "Apanasovka, Korenevsky District, Kursk Oblast")
.[\[161\]](#cite_note-162)

#### 19 August

Russia claimed that the Ukrainian military destroyed the third and last bridge over the Seym River in [Korenevsky District](/wiki/Korenevsky_District "Korenevsky District")
 leading to possible logistical strain on over 700 square kilometers of Russian territory.[\[162\]](#cite_note-163)

In his evening address, President Zelenskyy said that Ukrainian forces were in control of 92 settlements in Kursk Oblast and 1,250 square kilometers of Russian territory.[\[163\]](#cite_note-164)

#### 20 August

The Russian interior ministry warned residents of Bryansk, Kursk and Belgorod Oblasts against using online dating websites and security cameras, citing concerns of information being gathered by Ukrainian forces.[\[164\]](#cite_note-165)
 [Yunus-Bek Yevkurov](/wiki/Yunus-Bek_Yevkurov "Yunus-Bek Yevkurov")
, former head of [Ingushetia](/wiki/Ingushetia "Ingushetia")
 and incumbent deputy head of the Ministry of Defense was appointed as [Andrei Belousov](/wiki/Andrei_Belousov "Andrei Belousov")
's deputy in the Coordinating Council for the Security Issues of the Bordering Territories. The ministry stated, "After suffering losses, the Ukrainian sabotage group retreated to its territory, while some of the fighters attempted to establish a position on the territory adjacent to the state border, where they were blocked by Russian army units."[\[299\]](#cite_note-nva-300)
[\[300\]](#cite_note-guardian-301)
 President [Vladimir Putin](/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin")
 described the AFU's offensive into Kursk Oblast as a "large-scale provocation." He accused the "Kyiv regime" of "indiscriminately firing various types of weapons, including missiles, at civilian buildings, houses, and ambulances." Putin stated that he plans to meet with the heads of the security agencies, the Defense Ministry, and the [Federal Security Service](/wiki/Federal_Security_Service "Federal Security Service")
 (FSB).[\[72\]](#cite_note-NBC87-73)
[\[16\]](#cite_note-surface-17)

[State Duma](/wiki/State_Duma "State Duma")
 deputy and retired major general [Andrey Gurulyov](/wiki/Andrey_Gurulyov "Andrey Gurulyov")
 criticized the Russian army for failing to defend Kursk Oblast.[\[301\]](#cite_note-302)
 On 8 August, Gurulyov said in a television interview that the Russian military knew about the planned Ukrainian invasion of Kursk a month before it happened but "from the top came the order not to panic, and that those above know better."[\[302\]](#cite_note-303)

On 13 August, an immediate special meeting in the "[Arria format](/wiki/Arria_format "Arria format")
" of the [United Nations Security Council](/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council "United Nations Security Council")
 took place on request of Russia's Commissioner for Human Rights [Tatyana Moskalkova](/wiki/Tatyana_Moskalkova "Tatyana Moskalkova")
, who demanded to "condemn the actions of Ukraine" in relation to the events in Kursk Oblast.[\[303\]](#cite_note-304)

In response to the offensive, Putin has reportedly set deadlines for Russian forces to push Ukrainian troops out of Kursk Oblast, first by October 2024, which was then delayed to January 2025.[\[304\]](#cite_note-y851-305)
[\[305\]](#cite_note-g362-306)

Pro-Kremlin political analyst [Sergei Markov](/wiki/Sergei_Markov "Sergei Markov")
 told _The Washington Post_ that "the signal came from intelligence to the leadership, but ... She said that Ukraine would be conducting humanitarian operations in the area, that international humanitarian organizations would be allowed to enter, and that [safe corridors](/wiki/Humanitarian_corridor "Humanitarian corridor")
 would be opened for civilians to evacuate toward Ukraine or to other parts of Russia.[\[331\]](#cite_note-332)

On 7 September, [Kyrylo Budanov](/wiki/Kyrylo_Budanov "Kyrylo Budanov")
 noted that the offensive into Kursk had impacted and "complicated" Russian plans for an offensive in the upcoming winter.[\[332\]](#cite_note-ISW_September_7-333)

On 13 September, Zelenskyy acknowledged the Russian counter-attack but claimed there had been "no serious (Russian) success", adding that "It gave the results that, frankly speaking, we counted on" and reiterated claims that it had adversely affected Russian operations in Kharkiv and Donetsk Oblasts.[\[333\]](#cite_note-334)
[\[334\]](#cite_note-335)
[\[188\]](#cite_note-ISW_2024_09_13-189)

On 16 September, the Ukrainian government invited the United Nations and the [International Committee of the Red Cross](/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross "International Committee of the Red Cross")
 to inspect areas of Kursk Oblast that were under its control.[\[335\]](#cite_note-336)

### United States

The [White House](/wiki/White_House "White House")
 said that it was seeking an understanding from Ukraine regarding the incursion, adding that it had no advance knowledge of the attack.[\[53\]](#cite_note-Al_Jazeera_Third_Day-54)
 On 8 August, Deputy Pentagon Press Secretary [Sabrina Singh](/wiki/Sabrina_Singh "Sabrina Singh")
 stated that the incursion is consistent with the US policy on the use of weapons.[\[336\]](#cite_note-politico_20240809-337)
 On 12 August, [US National Security Council](/wiki/United_States_National_Security_Council "United States National Security Council")
 spokesperson [John Kirby](/wiki/John_Kirby_(admiral) "John Kirby (admiral)")
 called on Putin to withdraw his forces from Ukraine if he "doesn't like" the Ukrainian incursion in Kursk Oblast.[\[337\]](#cite_note-338)
 On 13 August, President [Joe Biden](/wiki/Joe_Biden "Joe Biden")
 said that the Ukrainian incursion was "creating a real dilemma" for Putin.[\[338\]](#cite_note-339)

### Germany

In response to the Kursk offensive, the German Foreign Ministry stated on 9 August that weapons transferred from Germany to Ukraine become the property of Ukraine and can be used by its armed forces as they deem necessary and correct."

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The claim is marked as NEI when there is not enough evidence to verify the claim or if the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory. 
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `misleading`: The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the claim or image is misrepresented in a wrong context or the necessary context is omitted. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way. If the claim refers to an image, it misrepresents the origin, content and/or meaning of the image.If the claim is a text-only claim, i.e. it does not refer to an image, it misrepresents the origin, content, and/or meaning of a statement.

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `not enough information`: The claim is marked as NEI when there is not enough evidence to verify the claim or if the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory. 
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `false`: The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `misleading`: The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the claim or image is misrepresented in a wrong context or the necessary context is omitted. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way. If the claim refers to an image, it misrepresents the origin, content and/or meaning of the image.If the claim is a text-only claim, i.e. it does not refer to an image, it misrepresents the origin, content, and/or meaning of a statement.
